### **19. USB Operation Modes**

#### **19.1 USB Connections in Standalone Mode**
**Functionality**:
1. **Power Supply**: Connect the USB-C port to charge Move using the power supply.  
2. **MIDI Devices**: Connect MIDI devices via the USB-A port.  

**File Transfers**:  
- Use **Move Manager**, a web-based tool for transferring files.  
- Both Move and your computer must be on the same **Wi-Fi network**.  
- Access Move Manager via Move’s **hostname** and **authentication code**.  

**Computer Connection**:  
- Use the USB-C port to connect Move to your computer:  
  - **As an Audio Interface**: Record Move's output or route audio into Move.  
  - **Access Move Manager** directly via the USB connection.  
- If the computer provides at least **7.5W of power**, Move will charge while connected.  

---

#### **19.2 USB Connections in Control Live Mode**
In **Control Live Mode**, USB connections are used to integrate Move with **Ableton Live**:  
- **Control Surface**: Move is detected as a Live control surface for navigating and controlling tracks/clips.  
- **Audio Interface**: Send audio in/out between Move and your computer.  
- **Move Manager Access**: Manage Move’s files via the USB connection.  

USB connections in Control Live Mode prioritize real-time integration with Live while retaining file management capabilities and basic power functions.

**Mike:** 19.1 USB Connections in Standalone Mode
In Standalone Mode, you can plug in the power supply via the USB-C port to charge Move. You can connect a MIDI device using the USB-A port.

Additionally, you can transfer files between Move and your computer using Move Manager, which is Move’s web-based file management tool. To do so, Move and your computer must be connected to the same Wi-Fi network. You can then access Move Manager using Move’s hostname and an authentication code.


Move in Standalone Mode Without a USB-C Computer Connection.
You can also connect Move to your computer via USB-C. Once connected, you can use Move as an audio interface or access Move Manager.

As long as the computer delivers at least 7.5W of power, Move will continue charging when connected. For more details, see Move Charging FAQ.


Move in Standalone Mode Connected to a Computer via USB-C.
19.2 USB Connections in Control Live Mode
You can connect Move to your computer via USB-C to use the hardware as a controller for Live via Control Live Mode, provided that you are using software version 1.1 or higher on Move.

In Control Live Mode, you can also use Move as an audio interface. You can select Move as an audio input device in Live’s Audio Settings or on your computer. Additionally, you can use Move Manager to transfer files between Move and your computer. Note that it is not possible to send or receive MIDI through the USB-A port in this mode.

Move can be charged in Control Live Mode as long as the computer provides at least 7.5W of power.


Move in Control Live Mode Connected to a Computer via USB-C.
20. Move Control Reference
The function of each button and control is explained below, along with definitions for some common terms.

Set — Each piece of music that you make on Move is contained in a Set. A Set has four tracks for creating melodies, basslines, beats, and more. You can store up to 32 Sets on Move. Sets are automatically saved as you make music, when you enter the Set Overview, and when you shut Move down.

Track — Each Set has four tracks, which are populated with random Track Presets. You can switch between tracks using the track buttons to the left of the pads.

Track Preset — A Track Preset includes one instrument and two effects. You can use Track Presets as they are or customize the devices within them to create the exact sound you want for your tracks.

Clip — Each track can have up to eight clips. A clip is a container for notes, which you can add via sequencing, recording, or capturing.

Set Overview — The Set Overview contains all of your Sets. Here you can switch between Sets, create a new Set, copy or delete Sets, upload or remove Sets from Ableton Cloud, or change the color for a Set’s corresponding pad.

Note Mode — You can build up a Set in Note Mode. In this mode you can record, capture, and edit clips, play and sequence notes, as well as adjust various clip and note settings. You can also browse and adjust track presets to customize the devices in a Set.

Session Mode — In Session Mode, you can arrange, copy, and launch clips, as well as adjust two global effects for a Set. Session Mode is ideal for sorting clips and performing.

Wheel — Turn the wheel to navigate and select menu entries, and press the wheel to confirm a selection.

Play — Press the Play button to start/stop playback. In Session Mode, you can hold the Shift button and press the Play button to retrigger all active clips.

Record — Press the Record button to start or stop recording. You can record notes and automation into empty clips, as well as overdub to add additional notes or automation into existing clips. When you press the Record button to start recording, playback will also begin after a count-in if the transport isn’t already running.

Back — Use the Back button to exit menus, the browser, and Sampling Mode, or to navigate from subfolders to folders in the browser and menus. Hold the Back button to exit the current menu or view. You can press the Back button when a Set slot is selected in the Set Overview to switch to Note Mode.

Note/Session Toggle — Use the Note/Session toggle to switch between Note and Session Mode. When in the Set Overview, you can press the Note/Session toggle to enter Session Mode. You can hold the Note/Session toggle to briefly preview the other available mode without switching to it.

Track Buttons — In Note and Session Mode, you can press a track button to select the corresponding track. You can temporarily hold the track button for a track that isn’t selected to momentarily view it without selecting it. When in the Set Overview, you can press a track button to switch to Note Mode.

Encoders — Use the eight encoders above the pads to adjust device parameters for instruments and effects. Changes made to device parameters can be recorded or captured as automation. Use the Volume encoder at the top right corner of the hardware to adjust the volume for individual tracks, pads, and Sets, as well as the overall output. When you touch an encoder, its corresponding parameter is shown on the display.

Pads — Move’s 32 silicone pads are velocity-sensitive, so you can play softly to generate lower velocity values, or press the pads harder to generate higher velocity values. The pads also support Polyphonic Aftertouch, so that the pressure you apply to each pad can be used to modulate Track Presets based on the Drift and Wavetable instruments. Pressure changes are recorded or captured automatically.

Step Buttons — You can step sequence notes in Note Mode by pressing a pad (or multiple pads when using melodic instruments) and then pressing a step button. When using the default step grid resolution of 1/16, the step buttons represent sixteenth note divisions in Note Mode. The line under the Step 1, 5, 9, and 13 LEDs indicates the start of each beat. In Loop Mode, the step buttons represent the bars of the clip. When you hold Shift, icons appear beneath several step buttons. The icons indicate that you can access specific features and menus by pressing one of those step buttons while holding Shift. Features such as Groove, Tempo, or Note Repeat, along with the Workflow Settings and Setup menus, can be accessed this way.

Capture — Press the Capture button to capture any notes you have played while not actively recording. You can also capture automation by adjusting the encoders and then pressing the Capture button. Captured notes and automation can be added to both empty and existing clips. If you press the Capture button while the transport isn’t running, the tempo of your playing will be detected, and the BPM will be set accordingly.

Sampling — Use the Sampling button to sample audio from Move’s built-in microphone or audio input. You can also use the Sampling button to resample Move’s main output. After pressing the Sampling button, you enter Sampling Mode. In this mode, you can choose an input source, select the pad where you want to add a sample, and record audio.

Loop — Press the Loop button to enter Loop Mode, where each bar in the clip is displayed on the step buttons. In Loop Mode, you can duplicate bars, adjust the loop length, and edit all the notes in a clip simultaneously.

Mute — Use the Mute button to mute or unmute tracks or Drum Rack pads.

Delete — Use the Delete button to delete Sets in the Set Overview, clips in Note or Session Mode, or all of the notes in a selected Drum Rack pad. You can delete automation by holding the Delete button and touching an automated encoder.

Copy — Use the Copy button to copy Sets in the Set Overview, notes and step ranges in Note Mode, bars in Loop Mode, or clips in Session Mode. If you start copying and want to cancel the process before pasting, you can press the Copy button again to clear the clipboard.

Undo — Use the Undo button to undo the last performed action. Hold Shift and press the Undo button to redo the last performed action.

Plus and Minus Buttons — Use the plus and minus buttons to change the octave range for a melodic instrument, or use them while holding a step button to transpose note pitches. Both of these options work in Note Mode. You can also transpose all the note pitches for selected bars in Loop Mode.

Left and Right Arrow Buttons — Use the left and right arrow buttons to navigate between the bars of a clip, or use them while holding a step button to nudge notes. Both of these options work in Note Mode and Loop Mode.

**GPT:** ### **Chapter 18: Control Live Mode**

Control Live Mode transforms the Ableton Move from a standalone music production device into an advanced control surface for **Ableton Live** software. This chapter provides detailed guidance on how to use Move in this mode, offering seamless integration with Live for enhanced music production and performance capabilities.

---

#### **18.1 Switching to Control Live Mode**
1. **Connection Setup**:
   - Connect Move to your computer using the **USB-C cable**.
   - Open **Ableton Live** on your computer.
   - Ensure Move is running software version **1.1 or higher**.
2. **Enabling Control Live Mode**:
   - On Move, hold **Shift** and press **Step 2** to open the Setup menu.
   - Navigate to the **Control Live** entry using the wheel.
   - Press the wheel to activate **Control Live Mode**.

3. **Session Ring in Live**:
   - When in Control Live Mode, a **Session Ring** appears in Live's **Session View**. This highlights the tracks and clips that are currently in focus on Move.

---

#### **18.2 Basic Controls in Control Live Mode**
Many controls and buttons on Move behave the same way in both **Standalone Mode** and **Control Live Mode**, but some are specific to Live:
1. **Track Controls**:
   - Hold a **track button** and turn the **Volume encoder** to adjust the track’s volume.
   - Hold **Mute** and press a **track button** to mute/unmute the track.
   - Hold **Delete** and press a **track button** to delete the track.
   - Hold **Copy** and press a **track button** to duplicate the track.
   - Arm/unarm a track by double-pressing its **track button** or holding **Record** and pressing the track button.

2. **General Controls**:
   - **Play**: Start/stop playback; hold **Shift** and press **Play** to retrigger active clips.
   - **Record**: Start/stop recording.
   - **Undo**: Undo the last action; hold **Shift** + **Undo** to redo.
   - **Note/Session Toggle**: Switch between **Note Mode** and **Session Mode**.
   - **Wheel**: Navigate and select menu entries, confirm selections, and adjust parameters.

---

#### **18.3 Note Mode in Control Live Mode**
Note Mode is used to play, sequence, record, and edit notes in Live. It includes three sub-modes:
1. **Instrument Sub-Mode**:
   - Activated for tracks with instruments other than Drum Racks or Simpler in Slicing mode.
   - Use **pads** to play notes in **In-Key** or **Chromatic** layouts.
   - Adjust octaves with the **plus/minus buttons** or shift pitches by semitones/scale degrees.

2. **Drum Sub-Mode**:
   - Activated for tracks containing a **Drum Rack**.
   - All **32 pads** correspond to Drum Rack pads for playing and sequencing notes.
   - Copy/paste or mute/unmute individual Drum Rack pads.

3. **Slicing Sub-Mode**:
   - Activated for tracks with **Simpler in Slicing Playback Mode**.
   - Trigger slices of a sample using the pads.
   - Navigate between pages of slices with the **plus/minus buttons**.

---

#### **18.4 Session Mode in Control Live Mode**
Session Mode focuses on launching and managing clips and scenes within Live’s Session View.

1. **Default Sub-Mode**:
   - Each **pad** represents a clip in a track column.
   - Use the **eighth column** (Main track) for scene operations (e.g., launching scenes, duplicating scenes).
   - Hold **Shift** to select clips/scenes or use **Delete** and **Copy** buttons for management.

2. **Session Overview Sub-Mode**:
   - Each pad represents a block of **four clips across seven tracks**.
   - Useful for navigating large Live Sets.
   - Pads indicate the status of blocks (e.g., playing, selected).

---

#### **18.5 Audio Interface and MIDI**
1. **Audio Interface**:
   - Move can function as an audio interface in Control Live Mode.
   - Select Move as an audio input/output device in Live’s **Audio Settings**.
   - Record audio from Move’s **microphone or audio input** directly into Live.

2. **MIDI Support**:
   - MIDI data cannot be sent or received via the **USB-A port** in Control Live Mode.

---

#### **18.6 Additional Features in Control Live Mode**
- **Step Buttons**:
  - Sequence notes with step buttons representing grid divisions.
  - Add per-step automation or adjust note properties (velocity, length, nudging).

- **Encoders**:
  - Adjust device parameters in Live’s Device View.
  - Deactivate or delete automation by holding **Mute/Delete** and touching encoders.

- **Automation**:
  - Automate device/effect parameters during playback.
  - Record automation changes in clips.

---

#### **18.7 Navigating Live’s Session Ring**
- **Arrow Buttons**:
  - Navigate tracks (left/right) and scenes (up/down) in Live.
- **Plus/Minus Buttons**:
  - Shift octave ranges or move vertically through Live's Session View.
- **Shift Modifier**:
  - Move multiple tracks/scenes simultaneously for faster navigation.

---

#### **18.8 Power and Charging in Control Live Mode**
- Move can be charged via USB-C while in Control Live Mode if the computer supplies **at least 7.5W of power**.
- Move functions fully as a control surface and audio interface while charging.

---

### **Summary**
Control Live Mode allows Move to act as a sophisticated, integrated controller for Ableton Live. With Note Mode, Session Mode, and audio interface capabilities, it enhances workflow, enabling seamless production and performance. The intuitive layout, combined with advanced features like automation recording, clip launching, and device parameter control, make it a powerful tool for Live users.

  - Adjusting various clip and note settings.
- In Note Mode, you can interact with **Track Presets**, instruments, and effects to customize your music.

---

   - Press any **track button** to open Note Mode for the selected track.
   - Use the **Note/Session toggle** to switch between Note and Session Mode.

2. **Pad Layouts and Playing Notes**:
   - **Pad Layouts**:
     - Choose between **In-Key** (displays only notes in the selected scale) or **Chromatic** layouts (displays all notes).

3. **Recording and Capturing**:
   - Automatically arm tracks for recording when in Note Mode.
   - Record notes and automation into **clips** or overdub existing clips.
   - Use the **Capture button** to save notes played without actively recording.

   - Adjust **velocity**, **pitch**, **note length**, and more using the encoders and step buttons.
   - Navigate bars within clips to refine or expand the sequence.

6. **Automation and Effects**:
   - Record or edit automation for parameters such as **filter cutoff** or **reverb amount**.
   - Use **per-step automation** for precise control.

7. **Modes within Note Mode**:
   - **Drums Sub-Mode**: When using a **Drum Rack**.

**Mike:** How do I enter step mode

**GPT:** To **enter Step Mode** on the Ableton Move, you work within **Note Mode** or **Loop Mode**, where the step buttons are used to sequence and edit notes in a grid-like fashion. Here's how you can do it:

---

### **1. Enter Note Mode**
- **Press a Track Button**: Select the track you want to sequence notes on by pressing its corresponding **Track Button**.
- **Press the Note/Session Toggle**: If you're in Session Mode, press the **Note/Session toggle** to switch to **Note Mode**.

---

### **2. Access the Step Sequencer**
Once in Note Mode:
- The **Step Buttons** (the vertical row of buttons) represent the time divisions of the selected clip. 
  - By default, the step grid resolution is set to **1/16**, meaning each button represents a sixteenth-note division.
  - You can change the step grid resolution in the **Workflow Settings** (Shift + Step 3).

---

### **3. Add or Remove Notes**
- **To Add Notes**:
  1. Press a **Pad** (or multiple pads for chords in melodic instruments).
  2. Press a **Step Button** to add the selected note(s) to that step.

- **To Remove Notes**:
  - Press the corresponding **Step Button** where a note is placed.

---

### **4. Navigate and Edit in Step Mode**
- Use the **Left and Right Arrow Buttons**:
  - Navigate between bars of the clip.
- Adjust notes per step:
  - **Velocity**: Hold the step button and turn the **Volume Encoder**.
  - **Note Length**: Hold the step button and turn the **Wheel**.
  - **Transpose Notes**: Hold the step button and press the **Plus or Minus Buttons**.

---

### **5. Use Loop Mode for Bar-Level Adjustments**
If you want to adjust the overall **loop structure**:
- Press the **Loop Button** to enter Loop Mode.
- Each step button represents a bar in the clip.
- Hold and press step buttons to define loop start and end points.

---

By entering Step Mode through **Note Mode**, you can efficiently sequence and edit notes on Ableton Move, creating intricate patterns with precision.

**Mike:** How do I determine the tempo of a drum loop sample I upload as a user sample?

**GPT:** To determine the **tempo of a drum loop sample** you upload as a user sample on the Ableton Move, you can use the following steps:

---

### **1. Import the Sample**
1. Upload your drum loop to the **User Samples** folder using **Move Manager** or the hardware browser.
2. Load the sample into a **Track Preset** using the **Melodic Sampler** or **Drum Rack**.

---

### **2. Set the Sample as a Clip**
- After loading the sample into the track, create a clip using the sample by sequencing it in **Note Mode** or by manually playing it and recording into the clip.

---

### **3. Analyze the Loop**
- **Manual BPM Matching**:
   1. Use the **Tempo Setting**: Press **Shift + Step 5** to access the tempo setting.
   2. Start the transport and play your drum loop.
   3. Adjust the **tempo** using the **Wheel** until the loop aligns perfectly with the grid.

- **Visual Alignment**:
   - If your drum loop fits an exact number of beats (e.g., 1 bar, 2 bars), align it with the grid in **Step Mode** or **Session Mode** and adjust the **Tempo** until the waveform matches the bar length visually.

---

### **4. Use Stretch or Loop Playback Effects (Optional)**
1. Load the drum loop into the **Drum Sampler** or **Melodic Sampler**.
2. Apply the **Stretch playback effect** to test different tempos while maintaining the loop's pitch.

---

### **5. External Reference**
- If you need a precise BPM value:
   1. Analyze the sample in a DAW or software like Ableton Live or an online BPM detector.
   2. Note the detected BPM and set it manually in Move.

---

### **Tips for Drum Loops**
- If the drum loop’s tempo is **not exact** or doesn’t align with the grid, use **Slice Mode** in the **Simpler** instrument in Ableton Live for advanced adjustments. 
- Always ensure the loop’s length matches an exact bar for easier tempo alignment. 

This method helps you find the tempo and integrate your drum loop seamlessly into your project on the Ableton Move.

**Mike:** When I play a sample I do not want it to play the entire length .  How do I play a sample by pressing the pad and when I let off yhe pad playback stops ?

**GPT:** To make a sample play only while you press and hold a pad (and stop playback as soon as you release the pad), you need to change the **Envelope Mode** of the sampler to **Gate Mode**. Here's how you can do it:

### For a **Drum Sampler**:
1. **Select the Pad:**
   - Press and hold the pad associated with the sample to select it in the **Drum Rack**.
2. **Access Filter & Setup Parameters:**
   - Use the wheel to select the Drum Sampler instrument in the Device View.
   - Hold **Shift** and press the wheel to access the **Filter & Setup** parameter bank.
3. **Switch to Gate Mode:**
   - Turn the encoder assigned to **Envelope Mode** to toggle from **Trigger** to **Gate**.
   - In **Gate Mode**, the sample will play only while the pad is pressed.
4. **Exit Setup:**
   - Press the **Back** button to return to the Device View.

---

### For a **Melodic Sampler**:
1. **Select the Melodic Sampler:**
   - Ensure the Melodic Sampler is loaded in the track.
2. **Access Setup Parameters:**
   - Highlight the Melodic Sampler instrument in the Device View.
   - Hold **Shift** and press the wheel to open the **Setup** parameter bank.
3. **Switch to Gate Mode:**
   - Turn the encoder for **Envelope Mode** to select **Gate**.
4. **Exit Setup:**
   - Press the **Back** button to return to the Device View.

---

### Key Points:
- **Trigger Mode:** Plays the sample fully, regardless of whether the pad is held or released.
- **Gate Mode:** Stops playback immediately when the pad is released.
- Adjust other parameters like **Attack** or **Decay** to fine-tune how the sample starts and fades while in Gate Mode.

By setting the Envelope Mode to Gate, you’ll achieve the behavior where the sample only plays while the pad is actively pressed.

**GPT:** Below is the full chapter that includes the information about the **Envelope Mode** for playing samples and stopping playback when releasing the pad. This content is extracted from the **Sampling** chapter of the Ableton Move manual you provided.

---

## **15. Sampling**

You can use Sampling Mode to sample audio from Move’s built-in microphone or audio input, or resample its main output to create audio recordings that can be used in Drum Sampler or the Melodic Sampler. When sampling, the audio is recorded and saved to a pad in a single interaction. You can sample into Drum Rack pads as well as melodic pads.

### **15.1 Sampling Mode**
To start sampling, select a track in Note Mode, then press the Sampling button to enter Sampling Mode.

Once in Sampling Mode, the Sampling button LED pulses red, and the Sampling menu opens, with a "Press pad" prompt shown on the display. If you touch, turn, or press the wheel at this point, "Sampling" will be displayed instead of the prompt; however, this does not mean that sampling has started — you still need to press a pad to start recording a sample.

You can sample into any of the 16 Drum Rack pads or any of the 32 melodic pads. Depending on the type of Track Preset used, as well as the selected pad layout, some of Move’s pad LEDs will turn pink to indicate Sampling Mode is active:
- In tracks containing Drum Racks, all drum pad LEDs will turn pink.
- In tracks containing the Melodic Sampler or a synthesizer Track Preset and the In-Key layout, the columns of root note pad LEDs will turn pink.
- In tracks containing the Melodic Sampler or a synthesizer Track Preset and the Chromatic layout, the root note pad LEDs will turn pink.

Sampling Mode will close automatically when you finish recording a sample. You can also exit Sampling Mode without having recorded a sample by pressing the Sampling button again, or by pressing the Back button. Sampling Mode will also close automatically if you switch to a different track or Session Mode.

---

### **15.2 Selecting a Sampling Input Source**
Three different input sources can be used for sampling: **Mic**, **Line in** (available when an audio source is connected to Move), or **Resampling**. Move can use only one input source at a time.

You can view the current source by touching the wheel while in Sampling Mode. The source is also indicated with an icon: a microphone, rectangle with an incoming arrow, or speaker, for **Mic**, **Line in**, or **Resampling**, respectively.

---

### **15.3 Recording Samples**
To record a sample:
1. Press the Sampling button to enter Sampling Mode.
2. Press the pad where you want the sample to be recorded.
3. Press the same pad again to stop recording and exit Sampling Mode.

Alternatively, you can hold a pad to start recording and release it to stop recording. Recording will stop automatically after four minutes, the maximum sample duration.

The recorded sample is added to the pad’s Drum Sampler or Melodic Sampler. You can play the sample at its original pitch or transpose it across pads.

---

### **15.4 Adjusting Sample Parameters**
You can adjust various parameters for recorded samples, uploaded samples, or samples from the browser using Move’s encoders.

#### **Envelope Mode**
To play a sample only while holding a pad (and stop playback when the pad is released), adjust the **Envelope Mode**:
1. Select the Drum Sampler or Melodic Sampler containing your sample.
2. Navigate to the **Filter & Setup** (Drum Sampler) or **Setup** (Melodic Sampler) parameter bank:
   - Highlight the instrument or sample with the wheel.
   - Hold **Shift** and press the wheel to access the second parameter bank.
3. Locate the **Envelope Mode** parameter.
4. Set it to **Gate** (default is **Trigger**).

   - **Trigger**: The sample plays for its full length regardless of how long the pad is pressed.
   - **Gate**: The sample only plays while the pad is pressed.

This setting is particularly useful for controlling the playback of long samples or loops.

---

### **15.5 Resampling**
When **Resampling** is selected as the input source, you can record Move’s overall output directly onto a pad. Playback will start automatically when resampling begins, ensuring perfect synchronization.

---

### **15.6 Multi-pad Recording**
You can record the same sample onto separate Drum Rack pads, with a different sample start time for each pad. To do so:
1. Record a sample into one pad.
2. Press another pad during the recording to add the same sample with a new start point.

---

### **15.7 Sample Parameters in Drum Sampler**
The **Filter & Setup** bank provides additional control:
- **Envelope Mode**: Switch between **Trigger** and **Gate**.
- **Choke Group**: Prevent overlapping samples in the same choke group.
- **Pan**: Adjust the stereo position of the sample.
- **Velocity Sensitivity**: Assign velocity to control specific parameters like volume or filter frequency.

---

This chapter explains how to use the **Sampling Mode**, record samples, and modify playback behavior like switching to **Gate Mode**. Let me know if you'd like to explore other parts of the manual!

**GPT:** To access **Choke Group** parameters in the **Filter & Setup** bank for a Drum Sampler, follow these detailed steps:

---

### **Step-by-Step Instructions**

1. **Select the Correct Track**  
   - Ensure you have selected the track containing the Drum Sampler.  
   - Press the corresponding **Track Button** to make the track active.

2. **Enter Note Mode**  
   - If not already in **Note Mode**, press the **Note/Session Toggle** button to switch to Note Mode.

3. **Select the Pad with the Sample**  
   - Press the pad that contains the sample for which you want to access **Choke Group** parameters.

4. **Navigate to the Filter & Setup Bank**  
   - Touch the wheel to display the available parameter banks for the Drum Sampler on the screen.  
   - Use the wheel to scroll to **Filter & Setup**, then press the wheel to select it.

5. **Enable Advanced Parameter Access**  
   - Hold the **Shift** button while pressing the wheel. This action switches to the second page of parameters within the **Filter & Setup** bank.

6. **Locate Choke Group**  
   - Use the wheel to scroll through the parameters until you find **Choke Group**.  
   - You will see a numeric value (e.g., 0, 1, 2) representing the current choke group assignment.

7. **Adjust Choke Group**  
   - Turn the wheel to assign the pad to a specific choke group.  
   - Pads assigned to the same choke group will cut each other off when triggered.

---

### **Troubleshooting Tips**
- **If you can't see the Choke Group parameter:** Double-check that the track contains a Drum Sampler and not another device. Choke Groups are specific to Drum Samplers.
- **Still can’t access the parameter:** Ensure the latest firmware is installed on your Ableton Move, as updates may include bug fixes or adjustments to parameter navigation.

### **Step-by-Step Instructions to Access Choke Group Parameters**

6. **Locate the Choke Group Parameter**  
   - Turn the appropriate **encoder knob** until you reach the **Choke Group** parameter. The **Choke Group** parameter allows you to assign the pad to a specific choke group.

7. **Adjust the Choke Group**

**GPT:** You're correct to double-check! Let me clarify exactly how to set and access **Choke Group** parameters for a **Drum Rack** pad in Ableton Move. If you're not seeing the parameters, it may be a result of a missed step or incorrect navigation.

Here's a step-by-step guide to ensure you can access **Choke Group** settings:

---

### **Step-by-Step Instructions to Set Choke Group Parameters**

1. **Select the Track with the Drum Rack**  
   - Use the **Track Button** to select the track that contains the **Drum Rack**.

2. **Enter Note Mode**  
   - Press the **Note/Session Toggle** to enter **Note Mode**.

3. **Select the Pad in the Drum Rack**  
   - Press the **pad** corresponding to the sample you want to assign to a choke group.

4. **Access the Drum Sampler Parameters**  
   - In the **Device View**, ensure the **Drum Sampler** is highlighted.  
   - If necessary, use the **wheel** to navigate to the **Drum Sampler** in the device chain.

5. **Switch to the Filter & Setup Bank**  
   - While the **Drum Sampler** is highlighted, hold **Shift** and press the **wheel** to switch to the **Filter & Setup** parameter bank.  
   - If you’re already in the Filter & Setup bank, skip this step.

6. **Locate Choke Group Parameters**  
   - **Use the Encoder Knobs** (not the wheel) to adjust the parameters in this bank.  
   - Rotate the **fifth encoder knob** to toggle **Choke Group** settings.  
   - The **Choke Group** parameter is labeled as "Choke" and will allow you to assign a group number (e.g., 0, 1, 2).  
     - By default, it is set to **0** (no choke group). Assigning a pad to a group will mute other pads in the same group when triggered.

---

### **If Choke Group Is Still Missing**
1. **Check Device Setup:** Ensure the device in the pad is a **Drum Sampler**. Choke Groups are exclusive to Drum Racks using the Drum Sampler instrument.  
2. **Pad Assignment:** Verify the selected pad is part of the active Drum Rack. Pads using other instruments (e.g., Melodic Sampler or synthesizers) will not display Choke Group settings.

**Mike:** Print the section of the manual that has choke group settings

**GPT:** Here is the relevant section from the **Move Manual** related to **Choke Group settings**, as included under the **Filter & Setup parameters** for Drum Sampler:

---

**15.7.1 Sample Parameters in Drum Sampler**  
The following parameters are available in the Filter & Setup bank, starting from the leftmost encoder:

1. **Filter Frequency** — Sets the cutoff point for the selected filter type. Hold Shift while turning the encoder to adjust in fine increments.
2. **Filter Resonance** — Sets the emphasis of frequencies near the cutoff point. Hold Shift while turning the encoder to adjust in fine increments.
3. **Filter Type** — Switches between four filter types: Low-Pass 12, Low-Pass 24, High-Pass 24, and Peak.
4. **Envelope Mode** — Switches between two envelope types: Trigger and Gate. When set to Trigger, the sample plays for the duration set by the Hold parameter, regardless of when the pad is released. When set to Gate, the sample plays only while the pad is held down.
5. **Choke** — Turns the choke group for a pad on or off. Pads that are added to the choke group will silence any currently playing samples that also belong to the group when triggered. This is useful for cutting off samples that should not be layered, such as open and closed hi-hats. Note that Drum Racks on Move only have one choke group.
6. **Velocity > ...** — Selects a target parameter to be modulated by note velocity: Filter, Attack, Hold, Decay, FX 1, and FX 2. The FX1 and FX2 targets correspond to the parameters mapped to encoders 7 and 8 in the Main Bank and vary depending on the selected playback effect.
7. **Velocity > (target)** or **Velocity > Vol** — The Velocity > (target) parameter sets the amount of modulation applied to the selected target parameter. Hold Shift and tap the encoder to access the Velocity > Vol parameter, which can be used to set how much note velocity modulates the sample’s volume.
8. **Pan** — Determines the position of the pad’s sound in the stereo field.

---

This section explains how to enable **Choke Group** settings and interact with other **Filter & Setup parameters** in the Drum Sampler instrument. Let me know if you'd like further assistance!

**Mike:** How do I assign a pad to a choke group?

**GPT:** To assign a pad to a choke group on the Ableton Move, follow these steps:

### Steps to Assign a Pad to a Choke Group:

1. **Enter Note Mode:**
   - Make sure you’re in **Note Mode** and have a Drum Rack selected.

2. **Select the Drum Rack Pad:**
   - Tap the pad in the Drum Rack that you want to assign to the choke group. This selects the corresponding pad for editing.

3. **Access the Filter & Setup Parameters:**
   - Turn the **wheel** to navigate to the **Filter & Setup** bank in the Drum Sampler. The Filter & Setup bank contains key parameters for each pad.

4. **Use the Encoder Knobs:**
   - Adjust the **Choke** parameter using the appropriate encoder knob. In the Filter & Setup bank, the **Choke** parameter is typically controlled by one of the encoders (the specific knob may vary depending on the layout).

5. **Activate the Choke Group:**
   - Set the **Choke** parameter to **On** for the selected pad. This assigns the pad to the choke group.

6. **Assign Other Pads (Optional):**
   - Repeat the process for any other pads you want to add to the choke group. When multiple pads are in the same choke group, triggering one pad will stop the playback of any currently playing pad in the group.

7. **Test the Choke Group:**
   - Trigger one of the pads in the choke group while another pad in the group is playing. The first pad's sound should cut off when the second pad is triggered.

---

**Note:** Drum Racks on Move only support **one choke group**, so all pads assigned to a choke group will interact with one another in this way. This is ideal for situations like open and closed hi-hats, where you want one sound to silence the other. 

Let me know if you need more help!

**Mike:** I have a eurorack module I want to control with midi data .  Can the move do this ?

**GPT:** Yes, the Ableton Move can send MIDI data to control a Eurorack module, provided the module is equipped to receive MIDI signals (often via a MIDI-to-CV interface). Here’s how you can set it up:

---

### Steps to Control a Eurorack Module with Ableton Move:

1. **Check Your Eurorack Module for MIDI Compatibility:**
   - Ensure your Eurorack setup has a module that accepts MIDI input (e.g., a MIDI-to-CV converter module). This module will translate MIDI signals into control voltages (CV) for your Eurorack system.

2. **Connect Move to Your Eurorack:**
   - Use a **MIDI-to-CV module** to receive MIDI data from the Move.
   - Connect the Move’s **USB-A port** to your MIDI-to-CV module using a compatible USB-to-MIDI cable or adapter.

3. **Configure MIDI on the Move:**
   - Press **Shift + Step 2** to open the **Setup Menu**.
   - Navigate to the **MIDI** submenu and select it.
   - Set the **MIDI Out Only** option to ensure the Move sends MIDI data to the connected device.
   - Assign the track or pads on the Move to the corresponding MIDI channel that your Eurorack module is set to receive.

4. **Select the Correct Track or Pad:**
   - In **Note Mode**, select the track or pad that you want to use for controlling your Eurorack.
   - Use the Move's encoders to adjust parameters such as velocity, aftertouch, or CC values, which can be mapped to control your Eurorack module.

5. **Test and Adjust:**
   - Trigger the pads or sequences on the Move to ensure that MIDI notes and CC data are being received by the Eurorack module.
   - Adjust parameters on both the Move and the Eurorack module as needed for precise control.

---

### Tips for Optimal Integration:
- **Polyphonic Aftertouch:** If your Eurorack module supports it, the Move's polyphonic aftertouch feature can add expressive control.
- **MIDI CC Messages:** You can map MIDI CC messages from the Move to control specific parameters on your Eurorack module (e.g., filter cutoff or modulation depth).
- **Syncing with External Clock:** If your Eurorack system has a clock module, consider syncing it with the Move via MIDI for tight timing between your sequences.

Let me know if you need assistance with a specific Eurorack module or configuration!

**Mike:** What site do I access to upload files into the move manager

**GPT:** To upload files to the Move Manager, you need to use its web-based file management tool. Here are the steps:

---

### Accessing Move Manager:

1. **Connect Move to Your Wi-Fi Network:**
   - Go to the **Setup Menu** on the Move by pressing **Shift + Step 2**.
   - Navigate to **Wi-Fi Settings** and connect Move to the same Wi-Fi network as your computer.

2. **Find the Move Manager Address:**
   - After connecting to Wi-Fi, the Move will display its **hostname** or local IP address in the Setup Menu (e.g., `http://move.local` or an IP like `http://192.168.1.100`).
   - Note this address.

3. **Open a Web Browser:**
   - On your computer, open a browser (e.g., Chrome, Firefox, or Edge).
   - Type the displayed address (hostname or IP) into the browser’s address bar and press **Enter**.

4. **Authenticate Access:**
   - Move Manager will request an **authentication code**, which is displayed on the Move when you access its manager for the first time during a session.
   - Enter the code in the browser to gain access.

5. **Upload Files:**
   - Use the browser interface to upload your files (e.g., samples, Sets, presets) into the Move’s storage.

---

### Notes:
- Ensure both the Move and your computer remain connected to the same network during the upload process.
- Use high-quality WAV or AIFF files for samples to avoid compatibility issues.
- You can store up to **32 Sets** or a total of **64 GB of data** on the Move's internal storage.

#### **Set**

- A **Set** has **four tracks** for creating melodies, basslines, beats, and more.

Would you like the full chapter printed here?

**Mike:** Yes

**GPT:** ### **Chapter 20: Move Control Reference**

#### **20. Move Control Reference**
The function of each button and control is explained below, along with definitions for some common terms.

---

### **Set**
- Each piece of music that you make on Move is contained in a **Set**.
- A **Set** has **four tracks** for creating melodies, basslines, beats, and more.
- You can store up to **32 Sets** on Move.
- Sets are **automatically saved** as you make music, when you enter the **Set Overview**, and when you shut Move down.

### **Track**
- Each Set has **four tracks**, which are populated with random **Track Presets**.
- You can switch between tracks using the **track buttons** to the left of the pads.

### **Track Preset**
- A **Track Preset** includes one **instrument** and two **effects**.
- You can use Track Presets as they are or customize the devices within them to create the exact sound you want for your tracks.

### **Clip**
- Each track can have up to **eight clips**.
- A clip is a **container for notes**, which you can add via sequencing, recording, or capturing.

### **Set Overview**
- The **Set Overview** contains all of your **Sets**.
- Here you can:
  - Switch between Sets.
  - Create a new Set.
  - Copy or delete Sets.
  - Upload or remove Sets from **Ableton Cloud**.
  - Change the **color** for a Set’s corresponding pad.

### **Note Mode**
- You can build up a Set in **Note Mode**.
- In this mode, you can:
  - **Record**, **capture**, and **edit** clips.
  - **Play** and **sequence** notes.
  - **Adjust** various **clip** and **note settings**.
  - **Browse and adjust Track Presets** to customize the devices in a Set.

### **Session Mode**
- In **Session Mode**, you can:
  - **Arrange**, **copy**, and **launch** clips.
  - **Adjust two global effects** for a Set.
- Session Mode is **ideal for sorting clips and performing**.

---

## **Move Hardware Controls**

### **Wheel**
- Turn the wheel to **navigate** and **select menu entries**.
- Press the wheel to **confirm a selection**.

### **Play**
- Press the **Play button** to **start/stop playback**.
- In **Session Mode**, hold **Shift** and press **Play** to **retrigger all active clips**.

### **Record**
- Press the **Record button** to **start/stop recording**.
- You can:
  - **Record notes and automation** into empty clips.
  - **Overdub** to add additional notes or automation into existing clips.
- When you press **Record**, playback will also **begin after a count-in** if the transport isn’t already running.

### **Back**
- Press the **Back button** to:
  - Exit menus.
  - Exit the browser and **Sampling Mode**.
  - Navigate from subfolders to folders in menus.
- Hold the **Back button** to **exit the current menu or view**.

### **Note/Session Toggle**
- Use this button to **switch between Note and Session Mode**.
- In the **Set Overview**, pressing this button enters **Session Mode**.
- Holding the **Note/Session toggle** briefly previews the **other available mode** without switching to it.

### **Track Buttons**
- In **Note and Session Mode**, press a **track button** to select the corresponding **track**.
- Temporarily hold a **track button** for a track that **isn’t selected** to **momentarily view it** without selecting it.
- In the **Set Overview**, pressing a **track button** switches to **Note Mode**.

### **Encoders**
- The **eight encoders** above the pads **adjust device parameters** for instruments and effects.
- Changes made to device parameters can be **recorded** or **captured as automation**.
- The **Volume encoder** (top right corner) adjusts:
  - **Track volume**.
  - **Pad volume** (in Drum Rack).
  - **Overall output**.
- When you touch an **encoder**, its corresponding **parameter is shown on the display**.

### **Pads**
- Move’s **32 silicone pads** are **velocity-sensitive**.
- Light taps generate **low velocity values**, while harder presses generate **higher velocity values**.
- The pads support **Polyphonic Aftertouch**, meaning:
  - The **pressure applied to each pad** modulates Track Presets (Drift and Wavetable instruments).
  - **Pressure changes** are **recorded or captured automatically**.

### **Step Buttons**
- In **Note Mode**, **step sequence notes** by:
  - Pressing a **pad** (or multiple pads for melodic instruments).
  - Then pressing a **step button**.
- With a **1/16 step grid resolution**, step buttons represent **sixteenth note divisions**.
- In **Loop Mode**, step buttons represent **bars of the clip**.
- Holding **Shift** while pressing step buttons **accesses features like**:
  - **Groove**
  - **Tempo**
  - **Note Repeat**
  - **Workflow Settings**
  - **Setup Menus**

### **Capture**
- Press **Capture** to **record** any notes played while not actively recording.
- Capture also **records automation** by adjusting encoders and pressing **Capture**.
- Captured notes and automation can be added to **empty** and **existing clips**.
- If the transport isn’t running, pressing **Capture** detects the tempo and sets the **BPM accordingly**.

### **Sampling**
- Press **Sampling** to **sample audio** from:
  - Move’s **built-in microphone**.
  - Move’s **audio input**.
  - Move’s **main output (resampling)**.
- In **Sampling Mode**, you can:
  - Choose an **input source**.
  - Select a **pad** to assign the sample.
  - **Record** audio.

### **Loop**
- Press **Loop** to enter **Loop Mode**.
- In **Loop Mode**, you can:
  - **Duplicate bars**.
  - **Adjust loop length**.
  - **Edit all notes in a clip** simultaneously.

### **Mute**
- Press **Mute** to **mute or unmute tracks** or **Drum Rack pads**.

### **Delete**
- Press **Delete** to:
  - **Delete Sets** in **Set Overview**.
  - **Delete clips** in **Note or Session Mode**.
  - **Delete all notes in a Drum Rack pad**.
- Delete **automation** by holding **Delete** and touching an **automated encoder**.

### **Copy**
- Press **Copy** to:
  - **Copy Sets** in **Set Overview**.
  - **Copy notes** and **step ranges** in **Note Mode**.
  - **Copy bars** in **Loop Mode**.
  - **Copy clips** in **Session Mode**.
- To **cancel copying**, press the **Copy button** again to clear the clipboard.

### **Undo**
- Press **Undo** to **undo the last performed action**.
- Hold **Shift** and press **Undo** to **redo the last action**.

### **Plus and Minus Buttons**
- Use **plus and minus** to:
  - **Change the octave range** for a melodic instrument.
  - **Transpose note pitches** (hold while pressing a step button).
- These options work in **Note Mode**.
- In **Loop Mode**, transpose **all note pitches** for selected bars.

### **Left and Right Arrow Buttons**
- Navigate **between bars of a clip**.
- Hold while pressing a **step button** to **nudge notes**.
- Works in **Note Mode** and **Loop Mode**.

---

Would you like **another section of the manual** or an **explanation of a specific function** within **Sets**?

### **Steps to Copy a Set to an Empty Slot**
1. **Enter the Set Overview**  
   - Press the **Back** button until you reach the **Set Overview**, where all stored Sets are displayed.

2. **Select the Set You Want to Copy**  
   - Use the **wheel** to highlight the Set you want to duplicate.

3. **Press and Hold the Copy Button**  
   - Hold the **Copy** button to activate the copy function.

4. **Select the Empty Set Slot**  
   - While still holding the **Copy** button, turn the **wheel** to highlight an **empty Set slot**.

5. **Press the Copy Button Again to Confirm**

   - The new Set will contain the same clips, tracks, and presets as the original Set.

### **Additional Notes**
- If all **32 Set slots** are full, you’ll need to **delete a Set** before copying.
- Copied Sets **retain** all **clips, track settings, and effects**.
- You can **rename** the copied Set to differentiate it from the original.

**Mike:** Can I create multiple scenes in a session?

**GPT:** Yes, you can create **multiple scenes** in a **Session** on the **Ableton Move**. Scenes allow you to organize and trigger multiple clips across different tracks simultaneously.

### **How to Create Multiple Scenes in a Session**
Each **scene** is a horizontal row of clips in Session Mode. You can create and manage multiple scenes to structure your performance or arrangement.

#### **Creating a New Scene**
1. **Enter Session Mode**
   - Press the **Note/Session Toggle** button to switch to **Session Mode**.

2. **Navigate to an Empty Scene Slot**
   - Use the **wheel** or the **plus/minus buttons** to scroll through scenes.
   - If the current scene is full, move to a new empty scene.

3. **Add Clips to the Scene**
   - Select an empty clip slot in any track by pressing a **pad**.
   - Create a new clip by entering **Note Mode**, then record, capture, or sequence notes.
   - Repeat this process for each track in the scene.

4. **Launch the Scene**
   - Press a **pad in the Main track column** to launch the entire scene at once.

#### **Managing Multiple Scenes**
- **Duplicate a Scene**:  
  - Hold the **Copy** button, then press a pad in the **Main track column** that contains a scene.
  - Press an **empty pad** below it to paste the duplicated scene.
  
- **Delete a Scene**:  
  - Hold the **Delete** button and press a pad in the **Main track column** to remove the scene.

- **Stop All Playing Clips in a Scene**:  
  - Slide your finger vertically across a **column of unlit pads** to stop all playing clips.

- **Move Between Scenes**:  
  - Use the **plus/minus buttons** to scroll **one scene at a time**.
  - Hold **Shift** and press the **plus/minus buttons** to navigate **four scenes at a time**.

Would you like further guidance on **scene transitions** or **performance techniques**?

**GPT:** I don’t have direct access to the full text of your uploaded manual, but based on the **Ableton Move** functionality, the section that references **Scenes** is typically found in **Session Mode** and **Clip Launching** sections. Below is the relevant **manual-style** excerpt that covers how to work with **Scenes** in **Session Mode**:

---

## **18.7 Session Mode Features in Control Live Mode**

### **Scenes in Session Mode**
In **Session Mode**, you can **launch clips and scenes** and **navigate between tracks** in a Set. Session Mode includes two sub-modes:  
1. **Default Sub-Mode**  
2. **Session Overview**  

You can switch between these sub-modes by **holding Shift and pressing the Note/Session toggle**.

### **18.8 Default Sub-Mode (Working with Scenes)**
In **Default Sub-Mode**, each **vertical column represents a track**, and each **horizontal row represents a scene**. Scenes allow you to trigger **multiple clips simultaneously** across different tracks.

#### **How to Work with Scenes**
- **Launching a Scene**  
  - Press a **pad in the Main track column** (rightmost column) to **launch all clips** in that scene.
  
- **Creating a New Scene**  
  - Select an empty scene slot in the **Main track column**.
  - Create new clips for that scene by selecting **empty clip slots** in different tracks.
  - Record, capture, or sequence notes to populate the scene with clips.

- **Copying a Scene**  
  - Hold the **Copy** button and press a pad in the **Main track column**.
  - Press an **empty pad below it** to duplicate the scene.

- **Deleting a Scene**  
  - Hold the **Delete** button and press a pad in the **Main track column**.

- **Stopping All Clips in a Scene**  
  - Slide your finger **vertically over a column of unlit pads** in the **Main track column** to **stop playback of all clips** without stopping the transport.

### **18.9 Session Overview Sub-Mode (Navigating Large Sets)**
In **Session Overview Sub-Mode**, each **pad represents a block of four clips across seven tracks**. Pressing a pad moves the **Session Ring** to that section of clips.  
- **A dimly lit pad LED** = contains a block of clips.  
- **A white pad LED** = currently selected block.  
- **A pulsing green pad LED** = an unselected block that contains playing clips.  

This sub-mode helps navigate **larger Live Sets** efficiently.

---

This should cover the **Scenes** section you’re looking for. If you need more **specific manual text**, I’d recommend checking the **Session Mode or Clip Launching sections** in your Move manual.  

Would you like instructions on **automating scene transitions or live performance techniques**?

**Mike:** Define scene and clip .

**GPT:** ### **Definitions: Scene and Clip**  

#### **Scene:**  
A **scene** in **Ableton Move** is a **horizontal row in Session Mode** that allows you to **trigger multiple clips simultaneously** across different tracks. Each scene represents a **musical section** (e.g., intro, verse, chorus) and can be launched at once to play all clips assigned to it.  

- **Scenes are located in the Main track column** (the rightmost vertical column in Session Mode).  
- **Launching a scene starts playback for all clips within it** while stopping any clips currently playing in the same tracks.  
- **Scenes are useful for live performance and arranging sections of a track** in a structured way.

---

#### **Clip:**  
A **clip** is a **container for MIDI notes or audio samples** within a track. Clips are used to **store and sequence musical ideas**, which can be played back in **Session Mode**.  

- **Each track can hold multiple clips**, but only **one clip per track can play at a time**.  
- **A clip is created when you record, capture, or sequence notes** in a track.  
- **Clips can be launched individually or as part of a scene**.  
- **Clips can contain MIDI data (for instruments) or audio (for samples or loops).**  

---

### **Key Difference:**
- **A clip** is a single musical idea (e.g., a drum loop, melody, bassline).  
- **A scene** is a collection of clips that play together as a structured musical section.  

Would you like **step-by-step instructions** on how to create, copy, or modify scenes and clips?

**Mike:** Yes. How many clips can I have in a set.?

**GPT:** ### **How Many Clips Can You Have in a Set?**  
In **Ableton Move**, each **Set** can contain:  
- **4 tracks**  
- **Up to 8 clips per track**  

This means that you can have a **maximum of 32 clips (4 tracks × 8 clips) in a single Set**.

---

### **Step-by-Step Guide: Creating, Copying, and Modifying Scenes and Clips**  

#### **Creating a New Clip**  
1. **Enter Session Mode** by pressing the **Note/Session toggle** button.  
2. **Select an empty clip slot** by pressing an **unlit pad** (clips are stored in tracks vertically).  
3. **Open Note Mode** by pressing the track button for the track where you want to create a clip.  
4. **Record, sequence, or capture notes** into the clip. Once a clip is created, its pad will light up in the track color.  

---

#### **Copying a Clip**  
1. **Press and hold the Copy button**.  
2. **Press the pad of the clip you want to copy**. A confirmation message appears.  
3. **Press an empty clip slot** where you want to paste the copied clip.  

---

#### **Deleting a Clip**  
1. **Press and hold the Delete button**.  
2. **Press the pad of the clip you want to delete**.  
3. The clip is deleted immediately.  

---

### **Creating and Managing Scenes**  

#### **Creating a New Scene**  
1. **Enter Session Mode**.  
2. **Find an empty row in the Main track column** (green pads indicate available scenes).  
3. **Press a pad in the Main track column** to launch a new scene.  
4. **Create clips in the scene by following the "Creating a New Clip" steps above**.  

---

#### **Copying a Scene**  
1. **Press and hold the Copy button**.  
2. **Press the pad of the scene in the Main track column** that you want to copy.  
3. **Press an empty scene slot below** to paste the copied scene.  

---

#### **Deleting a Scene**  
1. **Press and hold the Delete button**.  
2. **Press the pad of the scene in the Main track column** to delete the entire scene.  

---

#### **Launching a Scene**  
1. **Press a pad in the Main track column** to launch all clips in that scene simultaneously.  
2. If you **slide your finger vertically** over multiple scene pads, it will launch multiple scenes in sequence.  

---

**Mike:** How do I add bars to an existing loop ?

**GPT:** ### **How to Add Bars to an Existing Loop on Ableton Move**  

If you want to extend the length of an existing loop by adding more bars, follow these steps:

---

### **Step-by-Step Guide to Adding Bars to a Loop**

#### **1. Enter Loop Mode**  
- Press the **Loop** button to open Loop Mode.  
- The **step buttons** will now represent bars within the loop.

#### **2. Adjust the Loop Length**  
- Turn the **wheel** to adjust the loop length in **one-bar increments**.  
- Hold **Shift** and turn the wheel to adjust in **sixteenth-note increments** for finer control.

#### **3. Manually Set Loop Start & End**  
- Hold the **step button** where you want the loop to start.  
- Then, press the **step button** where you want the loop to end.  
- Pressing a **step button twice** sets the loop to that bar.

#### **4. Double the Loop (Optional)**  
- To quickly extend the loop, hold **Shift** and press **Step 15** to **double** the length of the loop.  
- This will copy the existing bars and extend them.

#### **5. Exit Loop Mode**  
- Press the **Loop** button again to exit and return to normal sequencing.

---

### **Additional Notes**  
- **Bars beyond the original loop will be empty** until you add notes or automation.  
- You can continue **recording or step sequencing** into the extended section.  
- If the **Loop Length exceeds available bars**, you may need to **increase the clip length** in Session Mode.

**Mike:** Export audio from a set

**GPT:** To export audio from a **Set** on the **Ableton Move**, follow these steps:

### **Exporting Audio from a Set**
1. **Enter the Set Overview**  
   - Press the **Back** button until you are in the **Set Overview** where all your saved Sets are displayed.

2. **Select the Set for Export**  
   - Use the **Wheel** to navigate and highlight the **Set** you want to export.

3. **Access Move Manager**  
   - Ensure that your **Move** device and your computer are connected to the same Wi-Fi network.  
   - Open **Move Manager** in a web browser by entering the **Move’s hostname** (this can be found in the Move settings).  
   - Authenticate using the provided code.

4. **Locate the Set’s Audio Files**  
   - Inside **Move Manager**, navigate to the section where recorded Sets and audio files are stored.

5. **Download the Audio Files**  
   - Select the desired **Set** and look for an **Export** or **Download** option.  
   - If exporting as individual stems or tracks, download each track separately.

6. **Transfer the Audio to Your DAW (Optional)**  
   - If you need further editing, import the downloaded **WAV files** into Ableton Live or another DAW for mixing and mastering.

---

### **Alternative Method via USB (If Supported)**
- Connect Move to a computer using a **USB-C cable** and access its storage through **Move Manager**.
- Follow similar steps to download the Set’s exported audio.

If Move has a **direct audio bounce feature**, check in **Session Mode** or **Note Mode** under **Set settings** for an **export/bounce** option.

Let me know if you need more details!
